  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_696ec183-7abf-405a-ae37-4fadc2e5d31a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Considering that this book was written five years before Twilight, it might be better to ask if Twilight is like the Sookie novels. Sookie is not an e<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Considering that this book was written five years before Twilight, it might be better to ask if Twilight is like the Sookie novels. Sookie is not an empty shell of a character like Bella, and though naive, she actually has a voice, a job, and a life before and during her Vampire liaison. <br />As Chelsea said, this is more adult and less YA. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          }
        });
      });

</script>    </div>

<div id="review_40125016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40125016" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/190396-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209310514p2/190396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40125016?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/190396-vanessa">Vanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40125016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2449606042410774947">After reading a succession of more serious books, I felt the need to read something light and trashy. As I discovered from reading this book, you should be careful what you wish for. Light? Yes. Trashy? Oh yes. Oh yes, yes, yes. But not in a good way - just trash, trash, trash.<br/><br/>It is hard to say what I disliked more about this book - the sophomoric writing, or the annoying, vapid, 2-d, Harlequin-romance-heroine-helpless-twit persona of Sookie Stackhouse. Sookie is a psychic, and this fact is used</span>
  <span id="freeText2449606042410774947" style="display:none">After reading a succession of more serious books, I felt the need to read something light and trashy. As I discovered from reading this book, you should be careful what you wish for. Light? Yes. Trashy? Oh yes. Oh yes, yes, yes. But not in a good way - just trash, trash, trash.<br /><br />It is hard to say what I disliked more about this book - the sophomoric writing, or the annoying, vapid, 2-d, Harlequin-romance-heroine-helpless-twit persona of Sookie Stackhouse. Sookie is a psychic, and this fact is used to explain everything from why she didn't do well at school and became a cocktail waitress to why she spends all of her free time sunbathing to why she can't see an obviously dangerous situation until she's up to her eyeballs in it. It does not, however, explain why she has such bad dress-sense (denim mini jumper dress with yellow bandana hair clip to impress the vampire who comes to dinner; Tweety Bird night gown that drives him wild with desire), or why her sexual naivete comes and goes like a rash - at times she is very confident about her sexual attractiveness (wearing "fuck me" red high heels etc) and other times wondering what Bill the vampire and all of the other men in Louisiana could possibly see in "l'il ole me".<br /><br />The sex scenes are either squirmingly bad or tedious. After reading two I just had to skip ahead a few pages any time sex with Sookie looked like it was going to rear its ugly and badly-written head.<br /><br />I know a lot of folks have enjoyed this series, and have devoured every book written by Charlaine Harris. From reading other reviews, it seems to be a very polarizing book. As for me, I could barely choke this one down and will look to satisfy my literary appetites elsewhere.<br /><br />3/28/10 - After having viewed the first two episodes of the HBO series "True Blood", I can now understand why people have gone bananas over this series of books. The show (what I've seen so far) is exceptionally good, thanks to a great cast and the writing talents of Alan Ball, who has turned a sow's ear into a silk purse. I can see how a reader might enjoy the books if they had viewed at least some of the series first and kept it in mind while reading Charlaine Harris's less than stellar prose. Unfortunately, that wasn't the case for me - and while I won't be reading any more of these books, I will continue to enjoy the show!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2449606042410774947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134286430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1453820235686095240"><br/>I started reading this series because I was currently watching True Blood and had developed a slight obsession with Eric. Since then, the books have become an absolute guilty pleasure of mine. They are not the best written and occasionally we get a little too much of what we don't care for (i.e. fairies and shifters) but amid the hot vamp sex and murder mysteries... who really notices those anyway??<br/><br/>Most characters have both annoying and redeeming qualities, but this is good - I never did like th</span>
  <span id="freeText1453820235686095240" style="display:none"><br />I started reading this series because I was currently watching True Blood and had developed a slight obsession with Eric. Since then, the books have become an absolute guilty pleasure of mine. They are not the best written and occasionally we get a little too much of what we don't care for (i.e. fairies and shifters) but amid the hot vamp sex and murder mysteries... who really notices those anyway??<br /><br />Most characters have both annoying and redeeming qualities, but this is good - I never did like the I-can-do-nothing-wrong hero/heroine. Plus Eric is <i>hot</i>... have I said this already?<br /><br />If you're looking for a life-changing experience, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38447" rel="nofollow noopener">The Handmaid's Tale</a>, but if you want something light, chick-lit style and kinda sexy too Sookie Stackhouse and her merry band of random supernatural creatures are where it's at. That probably sounded like a cheesy, promotional ad but what the hell. </span>

<div id="review_37462318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37462318" />
    <a title="Fabian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian"><img alt="Fabian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514061293p2/1036893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37462318?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian">Fabian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37462318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6751642622095668353">Stephenie Meyer has nuthin' on this woman (...understatement!). Harris has in one pinky all the talent of the aforementioned hack, and her huge fan base must take note. "Dead Until Dark" is a heavy middle finger to all those in deep love (& therefore those with questionable tastes) with the "Twilight" series.<br/><br/>This book reminds me that not all fiction has to be poetry. This one has a clear plot, it ties together all loose ends. It's enthralling, addictive, everything one wants in the PERFECT paper</span>
  <span id="freeText6751642622095668353" style="display:none">Stephenie Meyer has nuthin' on this woman (...understatement!). Harris has in one pinky all the talent of the aforementioned hack, and her huge fan base must take note. "Dead Until Dark" is a heavy middle finger to all those in deep love (&amp; therefore those with questionable tastes) with the "Twilight" series.<br /><br />This book reminds me that not all fiction has to be poetry. This one has a clear plot, it ties together all loose ends. It's enthralling, addictive, everything one wants in the PERFECT paperback novel. If only I knew about it before the HBO series "True Blood" (on which this book, book 1, is based) I would have definitely watch the series, but its occurred vice versa. The series explores characters, has more sex &amp; violence (duh, HBO) but does not touch the same ground this one cleverly hides within its first-look junk-lit verse.<br /><br />Sookie is the Everygirl, clever, lost, in love, found, frightened but curious and courageous. Bill the Vampire lacks the Lestatness of those that came after the Anne Rice novel, but it's okay. At least he's not one-dimensional like Edward Cullen.<br /><br />Everyone here, it seems, has secrets. The theme.<br /><br />There are dark inhabitants of the world, some don't have to be vampires or shapeshifters but humans with deep flaws. Once the mystery is solved (I solved this one waay before the climax), this theme comes to light. I wish I was a writer, important, like Charlaine Harris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6751642622095668353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4929635044068923920">🧛🏼‍♀️ <b>December 2014 buddy read</b> with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/25393430-sh3lly-not-all-those-who-wander-are-lost' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelly</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5892196-carole-s-random-life' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karly</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7125124-jess' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jess</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9371994-allison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Allison</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Monty Cupcake</a> 🧛🏼‍♀️<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>💀 <b>DNF</b> at 50%.<br/><br/><b>Sookie, Sookie, Sookie.</b> Because of you most of my friends either hate me or think I'm a total freak. <b>They think you're quirky, I think you're silly.</b> They think your story is better than candy, I think your story is the most uninteresting ever. <br/><br/><b>Sorry guys, I don't think this review is going to go well.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420295944ra/13201246.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I was recently told I was snarky and a cold-hearted, impatient cynic (yo</span>
  <span id="freeText4929635044068923920" style="display:none">🧛🏼‍♀️ <b>December 2014 buddy read</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/25393430-sh3lly-not-all-those-who-wander-are-lost" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelly</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5892196-carole-s-random-life" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja" rel="nofollow noopener">Karly</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7125124-jess" rel="nofollow noopener">Jess</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9371994-allison" rel="nofollow noopener">Allison</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake" rel="nofollow noopener">Monty Cupcake</a> 🧛🏼‍♀️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>💀 <b>DNF</b> at 50%.<br><br><b>Sookie, Sookie, Sookie.</b> Because of you most of my friends either hate me or think I'm a total freak. <b>They think you're quirky, I think you're silly.</b> They think your story is better than candy, I think your story is the most uninteresting ever. <br><br><b>Sorry guys, I don't think this review is going to go well.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420295944ra/13201246.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was recently told I was snarky and a cold-hearted, impatient cynic (you know who you are people!^^). <b>Guilty as charged.</b> Which might partly explain why I didn't like this. <b>Chick lit meets bad PNR as written by a 17 year old clearly is not me.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385869252ra/7247125.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>The story?</b> <br><br>Uninteresting at best. Apart from that? <b>Boring to death.</b> There is only so much I can read about Sookie's daily life: taking a shower, shaving her legs, plucking her eyebrows, putting on body lotion and deodorant… Seriously? <b>Arrrgggghhhhhh!!!!! Someone please shoot me!</b> Oh but wait, we also get to find out about fascinating stuff like her job at the bar or <b>Bill's shopping habits:</b> he gets his "khaki Dockers, green and brown striped golfing shirt, polished loafers, and thin brown socks" from Dillard's you see. <b>Fascinating stuff I tell you!</b> And don't get me started about Uncle Bartlett's prostate problems. <b>Wait wait wait!</b> Something is finally about to happen! Oops, sorry, it's only Sookie going to work again. <b>And it goes on and on and on and on…</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385869252ra/7247125.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Now for the corny stuff.</b><br><br><b>#1 Sookie and Bill</b> have known each other for about 5 seconds and they're already strolling hand in hand like two lovebirds. Okay, it's a bit silly but I can deal with it.<br><br><b>#2 <i>"Your dress is the color of your eyes."</i></b> Please tell me I did not just read this.<br><br><b>#3 <i>"His eyes looked at my body as if it were a drink of water on a desert dune."</i></b> Someone please shoot me. Again. <br><br>And it goes on and on and on and on… <b>I'm sorry. Mushy is not me.</b> <br><br><b>And mushy is just not sexy either.</b> Because Sookie &amp; Bill kissing and having sex is about as unsexy as it gets. What are these people made of? Stone? Cardboard? I don't think I've ever read such <b>boring, unexciting, ridiculous, badly written sex scenes.</b> But apparently Sookie doesn't notice because she's <i>"flying, flying, seeing white with gold streaks"</i> <b>{insert major eye roll here}.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385869252ra/7247125.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Sorry guys, I'm not done yet.</b><br><br><b>Defendant #1: Sookie</b><br><i>"I’m blond and blue-eyed and twenty-five, and my legs are strong and my bosom is substantial, and I have a waspy waistline."</i> <b>Are you kidding me?</b> Needless to say, Sookie and I got off to a bad start. <b>And it all went downhill from there.</b> The girl is silly, immature and overly naïve. I get that she's supposed to have been sheltered all her life but this is just too much. <b>The girl is supposed to be 25, not 15.</b> To make things worse she's as emotional as a stone. Did I say that already? <b>Oh well.</b><br><br><b>Defendant #2: Bill</b><br><b>Most boring vampire ever?</b> You got that right! I've never been a big vampire fan but this guy gives the word <b>dull</b> a whole new dimension. What with his <b>constant pity party</b>, corny ways, wanting to settle down, not wanting to drink blood from humans… <b>Get a life Bill!</b> A real badass vampire life! To make things worse he's as emotional as a stone. Did I say that already? <b>Oh well.</b><br><br><b>To think someone sold me this series</b> (yes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/25393430-sh3lly-not-all-those-who-wander-are-lost" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelly</a>, it's you I'm talking about) with images such as this one:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420304736i/13202455.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And I got Boring Bill instead? I am not pleased.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420304245ra/13202428.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This is not Urban Fantasy it's Boring Fantasy.</b> <br><br>By now I think you all realize <b>I slightly disliked this book.</b> But I'm a nice girl, I really mean no harm. <b>So please don't start unfriending me just yet guys! </b> I love you all and promise to behave from now on!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32059592" />
    <a title="Trin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/113980-trin"><img alt="Trin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181029461p2/113980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32059592?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trin" href="/user/show/113980-trin">Trin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=american-lit">american-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer32059592&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32059592" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6382230976904069079">Sigh. I tried to give this a fair chance, I really did. I went into it hopeful, despite some other negative reviews that I’ve read, because I quite liked the pilot for <i>True Blood</i>, the new HBO series based on these books. <i>Dark</i>, however, loses points from me right away because the two most interesting characters on the show—Sookie’s cranky best friend Tara, and Lafayette, the fabulous (in every sense of the word) chef at the bar where Sookie works—either completely don’t exist or have only the tin</span>
  <span id="freeText6382230976904069079" style="display:none">Sigh. I tried to give this a fair chance, I really did. I went into it hopeful, despite some other negative reviews that I’ve read, because I quite liked the pilot for <i>True Blood</i>, the new HBO series based on these books. <i>Dark</i>, however, loses points from me right away because the two most interesting characters on the show—Sookie’s cranky best friend Tara, and Lafayette, the fabulous (in every sense of the word) chef at the bar where Sookie works—either completely don’t exist or have only the tiniest of roles, respectively. Lame. Still, I find the basic premise Harris has cooked up intriguing: in this world, vampires have come “out of the coffin” and are public knowledge; they can drink Japanese-manufactured synthetic blood and have basic human rights. (On the show I believe they are still <i>working</i> toward those rights, but it hasn’t been made entirely clear.) That’s an idea that seems rich with symbolic significance that, correctly handled, could be truly fascinating.<br /><br />Instead, as Harris handles it, it’s just another boring romance between a powerful, possessive alpha male and his frail human woman who’s in need of his protection. Sookie isn’t, to be fair, as helpless and hopelessly devoted to her man as Bella <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Twilight</a> Swan is, but the basic power dynamic between her and Vampire Bill is still incredibly <i>boring</i>. In general, as a couple, they are boring. So there’s that dullness—bad enough—which Harris proceeds to combine with several shakes of sheer lunacy. Sookie completely under-reacts to incredibly traumatizing things, like waking up with a naked shapeshifter in her bed, or a loved one’s murder. She believes the PR that vampirism is a virus and is <i>really surprised</i> when someone points out that that doesn’t make sense considering that shapeshifters and telepathy also exist, and, you know, vampires can <i>fly</i>. Despite being telepathic, Sookie’s only able to solve the oh-so-complicated mystery when the killer attacks her. (Handy!) Oh, and Elvis shows up. I am not kidding.<br /><br />I wish I were, though. I also wish I was wrong when I say that I can predict pretty much exactly how the rest of this series will go, with Sookie, like a less lubricated Anita Blake, fighting off the affections of two (or more!) men and unable to make up her goddamn mind. Both of those men will devote their (un)lives to protecting her, and Sookie will say, “God! I’m a grown woman, I can take care of myself! I don’t need you to protect me!”—and then, instantly, need them to protect her. And then Kurt Cobain and Jimmy Hoffa will show up to hang out with Vampire Elvis.<br /><br />Gimme a break. I can only hope that the show proceeds to more interesting ground, because reading this book, all I could think was: been there, done that, have the lousy fang marks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6382230976904069079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_826641662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826641662" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826641662?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=darkness-horror-gothic">darkness-horror-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=love-and-romance">love-and-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826641662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8328509798146041618">The television show True Blood was better than this in every sense; it completely transcended it. Well, at least, before the fourth season hit and the writing went down the toilet. But that’s a separate issue altogether. The show took Charlaine Harris’s book and made the story better; it made it sexy and scary. But, let’s not forget that without this there would have been no show whatsoever. <br/><br/>So fans of the television show do owe a lot to Charlaine Harris. Her writing for me though can be summed </span>
  <span id="freeText8328509798146041618" style="display:none">The television show True Blood was better than this in every sense; it completely transcended it. Well, at least, before the fourth season hit and the writing went down the toilet. But that’s a separate issue altogether. The show took Charlaine Harris’s book and made the story better; it made it sexy and scary. But, let’s not forget that without this there would have been no show whatsoever. <br /><br />So fans of the television show do owe a lot to Charlaine Harris. Her writing for me though can be summed up in one word: tepid. She has the characters and some strong ideas, but she just can’t insert life into her prose. Where was the shock factor? Where were the cheap thrills and the melodrama? Normally I’d criticise a book for having these, but this one so desperately needed them! I didn’t find this story remotely exciting; it had no sense of drive, and, again, it lacked the sex appeal of the television show. Perhaps, I may have enjoyed this a little more if I’d read it before seeing all the blood and drama on the screen. Who knows? Either way this just didn’t hit the mark.<br /><br /><b> There is no atmosphere </b> <br /><br />Television Bill was a bit of an enigma, at least, he was at the start. He comes across as a brooding man, troubled by his past and his violent nature. Here, though, he’s just a bit boring. He doesn’t really have a lot about him. He seemed more computer geek than vampire solider. The writers of the show, undeniably, took his character and made it better; they made him interesting and devious. Some super fans will likely disagree with me. But ask yourself this, which Bill is more interesting to hear about? Which one would you rather turn at Merlot’s bar and grill giving you the eye and the fang? He carried with him a dark story, one the show slowly peeled back. <br /><br />Then there is the lack of antagonist. Sure, there’s a mysterious serial killer going around stabbing people to death. But, ultimately, he was dealt with rather easily. Again, to compare this to the show, the first season shadows Eric as a sort of bad guy. It was so much more entertaining! I have read much further than this book in the series. In my mid to late teens I managed to get through most of them, and I didn’t really enjoy any of them. I’m not sure why I kept reading them to be honest; it was likely due to a lack of reading material and funds to buy something better. <br /><br />True Blood is far from being the peak of television artistry; however, it can be enjoyed for what it is: a dark and mysterious fantasy romance that depicts weird and wonderful characters struggling though their fucked up lives. This here is the story of just Sookie Stackhouse whereas True Blood expands on the side characters and fleshes them out; they were the ones that make it fun. Sookie is just dull, her life is dull, and this book is dull. Even after all these years I can still taste the blandness of the writing. If my seventeen year old self, a self who had read less than twenty books in his life hated this, I dread to think how I would react to it now if I was reading it for the first time. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8328509798146041618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_20287532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20287532" />
    <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days"><img alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20287532?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20287532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18088450973430370052">I'd never heard of these books until a few months ago, and as usual, once one person recommends them, everyone seems to be talking about them, you see them everywhere, and you get curious. They're in the fantasy section, though for some bizarre reason I was under the impression, at first, that they were YA and silly. They are fun, but they are definitely for adults. The vampire/mystery style reminds me of the one Anita Blake book I read, the first one, which was horrible (can't say that enough t</span>
  <span id="freeText18088450973430370052" style="display:none">I'd never heard of these books until a few months ago, and as usual, once one person recommends them, everyone seems to be talking about them, you see them everywhere, and you get curious. They're in the fantasy section, though for some bizarre reason I was under the impression, at first, that they were YA and silly. They are fun, but they are definitely for adults. The vampire/mystery style reminds me of the one Anita Blake book I read, the first one, which was horrible (can't say that enough times) - the similarities aren't obvious or anything, but perhaps because <i>Dead Until Dark</i> isn't paranormal romance, and it's not like <i>The Turning</i> or the Black Dagger Brotherhood books, Anita Blake is the closest comparison.<br /><br />Oh but this book is soooooo much better! After a slightly rocky start in which the writing confused me a bit (something that also reminded me of <i>Guilty Pleasures</i>, perhaps unfairly), the story really gets going and in new and surprising ways.<br /><br />Sookie Stackhouse is a waitress at a bar in Bon Temps in Louisiana. She has what she calls a disability: she can read minds. She's spent her young life trying to guard against the babble of other people's thoughts, and because of the level of concentration that takes she never did particularly well at school and never went to uni. But she likes working at Merlotte's, likes living with her Gran since her parents died, even though she can't have a relationship - it wouldn't be fun hearing what a man thought of you while being "intimate", would it?<br /><br />She's also fascinated by vampires and has been waiting to meet one since they "came out of the coffin", so to speak, and became legal citizens. One night her wish comes true: a vampire called Bill (!) comes into Merlotte's and, joy of joys, his mind is silent. She can't hear a thing. Finally a man - an undead man, true - she can relax with.<br /><br />But while Sookie and Bill are trying to have a normal relationship, working class women are being murdered in the area and while at first it looks like vampire work, soon the police are looking at Sookie's womanising brother Jason. On top of that, the most powerful (and dead gorgeous) vampire in the area, Eric, has his eye on Sookie and her ability for his own uses.<br /><br /><i>Dead Until Dark</i> is a great mix of urban fantasy and mystery, and the crime side of the story didn't bore me a bit. I loved Bill, he was kinda adorable while also a bit unpredictable and scary (very nice), and while I didn't understand <i>all</i> the expressions I've seen enough movies set in southern US states that I could picture the people, places and culture fairly well. The book could have done with better proof-reading to catch all those missing prepositions and, at one point, an interesting way of spelling "complexion". There were also a few times where Sookie, who narrates, is musing about something and then another characters replies - it threw me off because it wasn't all that clear that she'd voiced her thoughts.<br /><br />Sookie is a great protagonist, lively, fiesty, quirky and strong without being stubborn and bitchy, and her telepathy makes her especially interesting. She's definitely one of the better heroines of vampire novels I've come across to date. I loved Sam too, and Dean was great! Oh and the Elvis thing was funny too, though I was a bit slow in catching on. Anyway, if vampire books aren't your usual cup of tea, you might want to try this series because it's very enjoyable and fast-paced, yet with nice slow moments where you get to enjoy and understand the characters (so good character development, always important). So I guess this means I'm joining the Sookie Stackhouse bandwagon?</span>
  <a data-text-id="18088450973430370052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10459656163039589275">I might have enjoyed this one more if Sookie was a bit more relatable. In a paranormal romance, the reader is supposed to be able to project themselves into the main character, right? I mean, we pretend like that's not the point but that's kinda sorta really the point. <br/>But Sookie is so emotionally distant and half the time I can't even tell if she's happy or sad or angry or what. Her motivations are hard to decipher from the text. <br/><br/>Perhaps I misjudged the intent of the book; maybe it was written </span>
  <span id="freeText10459656163039589275" style="display:none">I might have enjoyed this one more if Sookie was a bit more relatable. In a paranormal romance, the reader is supposed to be able to project themselves into the main character, right? I mean, we pretend like that's not the point but that's kinda sorta really the point. <br>But Sookie is so emotionally distant and half the time I can't even tell if she's happy or sad or angry or what. Her motivations are hard to decipher from the text. <br><br>Perhaps I misjudged the intent of the book; maybe it was written more as a murder-mystery than a PNR flick. But, having watched True Blood before starting this series, my expectations going in were of steaminess and drama with a little spicy mystery mixed in. I was left a little disappointed.<br><br>However I'm still soldiering on with the series because <i>THIS</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508712748i/24246843._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>MMMMmmmmmmmm. I want to get to know Charlaine's version of Eric Northman.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1880731862?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile">Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880731862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12406763022741227035">3.5 stars rounded up. I enjoyed this much more than I thought I would. I’m not a fan of smut at ALL, so I was expecting this to be a straight up romance novel. I’m happy to report that it was definitely literary enough to appeal. The world that the author created is fascinating and I’m loving learning more about it. On to the next!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2242896529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242896529" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2242896529?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6316683-dead-until-dark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2242896529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11173438626333250593"><b>*** 3.44 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the folks @ FBR... </b><br/><br/>I finally got to read a book that has been on my TBR for many, many years. I own the complete series and have been thinking about starting, only every time I get distracted by something newer and shinier, thus I have to thank FBR for having a buddy read scheduled, because I have a feeling if I didn't get to it now, I never would have... <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"...“This was pretty exotic stuff for a telepathic barmaid from northern Louisiana.” ..."</i>
</b><br/><br/>This was a short an</span>
  <span id="freeText11173438626333250593" style="display:none"><b>*** 3.44 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the folks @ FBR... </b><br /><br />I finally got to read a book that has been on my TBR for many, many years. I own the complete series and have been thinking about starting, only every time I get distracted by something newer and shinier, thus I have to thank FBR for having a buddy read scheduled, because I have a feeling if I didn't get to it now, I never would have... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“This was pretty exotic stuff for a telepathic barmaid from northern Louisiana.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />This was a short and quick read, which dates itself a bit, but still gives plenty of entertainment to be worth the time. Sookie is a waitress in a small town Louisiana, who happens to be a telepath valiantly trying to shield her mind from all the thoughts other people project. Of course, her "disability" makes her the weird girl of the town, and when she meets the first vampire to try to settle openly in the neighborhood, she feels she can relate to him as an outsider... Bonus, he is hot and she can't read his thoughts, thus he becomes like catnip to a kitten to her. As they get to know each other, weird murders inflict the township and anger and mistrust against the nice vamp, his name is Bill, by the way, grow, while suspicion against Sookie 's brother also find foundations. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“The world seemed a bad and terrible place, all its denizens suspect, and I the lamb<br />wandering through the valley of death with a bell around my neck.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I am aware that there has been an HBO series based on this series, but I am of the minority who never saw it nor had any clue about the books. As a novice and having no expectations, I actually enjoyed it, despite its simplicity and brevity, maybe even because of them. I did feel that Sookie could be a bit annoying with her snowflake syndrome and "purity of soul", but it was not prevalent and I guess I could fathom there being 25 years old gorgeous virgins with minimal tolerance for bad language while working in a country bar, but I have personally never known any... 😈😇😈😇😈😇<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“It was one of God's jokes that such a dumb mind had been put in such an eloquent body.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />This is an old school Urban Fantasy and it will be perfect for the fans of the genre or those who would like to get acquainted with it. I am told it is very different from the TV show, for those who would be interested because of it. <br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful books to come!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11173438626333250593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_351649875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351649875" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351649875?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6316683-dead-until-dark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=weres-shapeshifters">weres-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorite-secondary-characters">favorite-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=jerk-of-my-dreams">jerk-of-my-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=esp">esp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=best-series">best-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351649875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4927938629217094313"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000OCXHRW/ref=as_li_ss_il?caller=Goodreads&callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6316683-dead-until-dark&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=62567a6b5caf1ab64fcfca9fbe30f829' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506791355i/24053429.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506791354i/24053428.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2x4G9ZN'>http://amzn.to/2x4G9ZN</a><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/03/review-dead-until-dark-by-charlaine-harris.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I basically had two separate lives growing up. My main life involved my nurse mother, my pharmacist (legal) father, and two of my three sisters, all living a suburban life just outside of Charlotte, NC. My secondary life involved my biological father and his entire family which <i>was</i> (they’ve since departed) headquartered in Bon Aqua (pronounced “ACK-qua”), TN. Bon Aqua, thusly named for the water that locals li</span>
  <span id="freeText4927938629217094313" style="display:none"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b> <br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000OCXHRW/ref=as_li_ss_il?caller=Goodreads&amp;callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6316683-dead-until-dark&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=62567a6b5caf1ab64fcfca9fbe30f829" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506791355i/24053429.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506791354i/24053428.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2x4G9ZN">http://amzn.to/2x4G9ZN</a><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/03/review-dead-until-dark-by-charlaine-harris.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>I basically had two separate lives growing up. My main life involved my nurse mother, my pharmacist (legal) father, and two of my three sisters, all living a suburban life just outside of Charlotte, NC. My secondary life involved my biological father and his entire family which <i>was</i> (they’ve since departed) headquartered in Bon Aqua (pronounced “ACK-qua”), TN. Bon Aqua, thusly named for the water that locals lineup in their pickup-trucks to collect, with their empty milk jugs, flowing out of a rusted pipe in the ground. True story.<br><br>I think that’s one of the reasons I like Charlaine Harris’ Sookie Stackhouse series so much—b/c I can relate. I grew up hearing people say things like, <i>“Sure enough, some sumbitch, scuse me, was sneaking around the house,”</i> which is what Bubba (and by “Bubba” I mean ELVIS) said after he scared away the creeper from Sookie’s house. And I am intimately acquainted with the small-minded prejudices that seem to thrive in small towns. My family, for the most part, isn’t like that, but you can’t grow up in that kind of place without hearing some very politically incorrect terms and phrases tossed around. The kind of place where if you take issue with said politically incorrect terms and phrases, you’re either “uppity” if you’re a woman, or a “woman” if you’re a man.<br><br>So it’s nice to see someone like Sookie—a college degree-less, “barmaid” who has been whispered and gossiped about her entire life b/c of her “disability”, come out ahead of her “betters.”<br><br>Better than nice. I bloody LOVE it.<br><br>No, Sookie didn’t go to college. Kind of hard to continue her education when she’s a telepath who can’t keep everyone else’s thoughts out of her head without extreme effort. So much effort that she has nothing left to devote to things like paying attention in class. And yes, Sookie is a SERVER (fortheloveofgod). I was too when I was in school. But Sookie is <i>not</i> an idiot, and though she does admittedly have her less-than-stellar moments, Harris ultimately creates a highly capable woman in her.<br><br>So for the three (or so) of you that haven’t read the books or watched <i>True Blood</i> yet, <i>Dead Until Dark</i> takes place in a world just like ours. With one exception—the Japanese have created and patented synthetic blood, ending blood shortages for medical facilities, AND prompting vampires to come out of the <i>coffin</i>, so to speak.<br><br>*snickers*<br><br>The vampires took this action b/c they felt they would be well-received now that humans no longer had to fear for their lives (in regards to vampires). Vampires could subsist on the manufactured blood, protecting humans from their thirst.<br><br>Things are rarely so simple.<br><br>Incidentally, the vampires’ party-line is that they are the victims of a virus that gives them the appearance of being dead for three(ish) days, after which they rise with allergies to things like garlic and sunlight, silver and . . . holy water . . .<br><br>*snorts*<br><br>They are received with equal parts fear and awe.<br><br>So Sookie is thrilled when a vampire walks into Merlotte’s, the bar where she works, and sits in her section. And when she realizes that she can’t hear the vampire’s thoughts she is shocked and delighted. But just b/c she can’t hear the vampire’s thoughts, doesn’t mean she can’t hear the thoughts of two bar patrons intent on draining the vampire for his blood. When she follows the three of them out to the parking lot and rescues Bill (the vampire), she begins the series of events that lead to her romantic involvement a vampire.<br><br>And the timing couldn’t be worse b/c someone is strangling women in Bon Temps (where Sookie lives) who are known to associate with vampires . . .<br><br>The <i>Sookie Stackhouse</i> series by Charlaine Harris was one of the first Urban Fantasy series I ever read, and no matter how disappointed I was with how it ended last year, I don’t think I’ll ever stop loving Sookie. <i>Dead Until Dark</i> was the beginning of that love, and up until book 10 or 11 that love only grew (and 10 or 11 out of 13 ain’t bad). This series is one that every lover of Urban Fantasy should have under their belt, so if you haven’t already, what are you waiting for? You’ve got nearly a dozen books before you need to be worried about anything, and if you simply can’t accept the ending, I’m sure you can find a fanfic somewhere that will do your dreams justice. Don’t miss out on Sookie altogether just b/c she doesn’t live HEA with the crowd favorite. ALSO--by the time you get to book 13, the "crowd favorite" could be one of a couple different characters b/c one of them turned into such an a**hole! So, if you didn't read that far, don't automatically make assumptions (like I did when I assumed everyone knew this already)!<br><br>*****I'm seeing now that I didn't explain why I only gave this book 3.5 stars when I only had good things to say about it. My bad. The reason is that there was a LOT of relationship angst. I can tell that Harris was trying to be realistic, and that's admirable. Real relationships DO have problems. BUT no one wants to hear about everybody else's everyday, nit-picky relationship issues. It's dull. And obnoxious. Which is how I felt about most of Bill and Sookie's relationship. Oh, they had their good moments too, but then there were all the times Bill took "matters" into his own hands, and all the little misunderstandings, etc. Just . . . enough already. SO. That's why only 3.5 stars. It should come as no surprise that I did not miss Bill at ALL once he was gone.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351709492" rel="nofollow noopener">Living Dead in Dallas (Sookie Stackhouse #2)</a>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4927938629217094313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13173339095046929353" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br /> This is the first book in the Sookie Stackhouse Series and I did enjoy it but I don't think I will be continuing with this series. It just did not <br />really excite me so much. I guess the main reason why is because I really do not care for vampire stories too much. I thought this would be an exception since there was a mystery in the book, and that was the part that I enjoyed.<br /><br /> Welcome to the small town of Bon Temps in Louisiana, where a mid twenty, blonde, blue-eyed waitress named Sookie Stackhouse calls home. But she's no ordinary waitress, she has a disability. She's a telepath. This makes life a little difficult for Sookie, particularly the dating part. Imagine ‘hearing’ all your dates thoughts, not always a desirable thing, especially if there scrutinizing you.<br /><br />Then one day a stranger arrives in town. He is tall, dark and handsome. And the best part is that, unlike everyone else, Sookie cannot hear his thoughts. But he is not perfect; he is pale, fanged and dead. Enter Bill Compton, vampire.<br /><br />What follows is a fun and entertaining story, mixing romance, mystery and vampires, as Sookie and Bill begin a relationship, attempt to solve a number of murders that have coincidently occurred with the arrival of Bill into town, not to mention land her brother in jail, and also begins for her a new, and somewhat unwanted, career with the vampires of Louisiana.<br /><br />It’s an enjoyable and effortless read, a book you can easily lose yourself in. </span>

  <span id="freeText6006530394265334221" style="display:none">I enjoyed Dead Until Dark more than I thought, I had only watched the first season of True Blood and I liked it alright but I never felt any desire to watch any other seasons. Season one stays very loyal to the book. I did miss Tara, she was my favorite character from season one. Since I remembered the first season I knew who the killer was but that didn't bother me because this book was just so much fun to read. <br /><br />As with the show I found Sookie to be annoying but not enough to dampen my enjoyment of the book. Bill was just as boring in the book as I remembered him from the show. I'm hoping in the next book I get more Eric and maybe Bill grows a personality. The book didn't have as much sex as I thought but it was just as gory as I thought. <br /><br />Recommended for fans of Laurell Hamilton and Anne Rice. This is not Twilight, so if you like your vampires sparkling and brooding this is not the series for you. <br /><br />2018 Badass Books Reading Challenge: A book turned Tv show you've seen but never read.<br />Around the Year In 52 Books: A book written in first person perspective.<br />Read-A-Thin May Challenge: Read a book you've been meaning to get to but haven't.</span>

<div id="review_459241974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459241974" />
    <a title="Scott Sigler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1782315-scott-sigler"><img alt="Scott Sigler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442455917p2/1782315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459241974?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Sigler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Sigler" href="/user/show/1782315-scott-sigler">Scott Sigler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459241974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17022432083378333984">First off, paranormal fiction of any stripe really isn't my bag. I'm more of a hard-science/horror, horror/thriller kind of a guy. <br/><br/>I'm a big fan of the TRUE BLOOD television series. My wife tricked me into watching it, because I was convinced I "couldn't possibly like yet another kissy-vampire show." Well, I was wrong; I got hooked on the campy fun of TRUE BLOOD right off the bat. <br/><br/>Since I'm an author and have high hopes of seeing one of my own books turned into a series someday, I picked up the </span>
  <span id="freeText17022432083378333984" style="display:none">First off, paranormal fiction of any stripe really isn't my bag. I'm more of a hard-science/horror, horror/thriller kind of a guy. <br /><br />I'm a big fan of the TRUE BLOOD television series. My wife tricked me into watching it, because I was convinced I "couldn't possibly like yet another kissy-vampire show." Well, I was wrong; I got hooked on the campy fun of TRUE BLOOD right off the bat. <br /><br />Since I'm an author and have high hopes of seeing one of my own books turned into a series someday, I picked up the first DEXTER book and DEAD UNTIL DARK to see how TV writers adapted novels for the small screen. DEXTER blew me away and still ranks as one of the most brilliant "high concept" ideas in horror fiction.<br /><br />Then I read DEAD UNTIL DARK, and you know what? It's fantastic. I need to get over my snooty attitude about paranormal romance, because this is just a flat-out good story.<br /><br />Harris creates a fantastic main character. Sookie Stackhouse is full of flaws and doubts, and at the same time is perfectly content in her normal life. As content as she can be, considering her telepathic abilities. The normalcy and neuroses of Sookie make her instantly "real." I was empathizing with her before any of the madness started, and that let me slip into the story and accept all the paranormal activity: I mean, it's not happening to some character, it's happening to my rational friend Sookie, so it's okay to believe in it.<br /><br />Bottom line: loved the book, loved the character. The novel is fun, sexy and puts a great skin on a Down South murder mystery. It's no wonder this series is so popular. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17022432083378333984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Evgeny by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715402887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10778362789752032080">A group read with my GR buddies. <br/><br/>Sookie Stackhouse has a disability - at least she thinks she has one. She can read minds and she always has to block this ability of hers to keep herself from going crazy from constant buzz of thoughts from everywhere. She also wants to meet a vampire, so when one finally walks into the bar she works as a waitress in, she literally jumps at him the way poor creature does not stand a chance. <br/><br/>For people who read Twilight I do not need to tell anything more as this </span>
  <span id="freeText10778362789752032080" style="display:none">A group read with my GR buddies. <br /><br />Sookie Stackhouse has a disability - at least she thinks she has one. She can read minds and she always has to block this ability of hers to keep herself from going crazy from constant buzz of thoughts from everywhere. She also wants to meet a vampire, so when one finally walks into the bar she works as a waitress in, she literally jumps at him the way poor creature does not stand a chance. <br /><br />For people who read Twilight I do not need to tell anything more as this most definitely was a book which heavily inspired Stephenie Meyer. I found two differences between the books. Sookie is more fleshed out than Bella Swan and unlike Twilight universe the vampires do not sparkle in this series; they glow. <br /><br />This basically is the whole review. If you like Twilight this might be your cap of tea. If you did not there is still hope for you - as I mentioned Sookie is a fairly interesting character on her own. There is also a mystery in the book to keep things more exciting, but to be fair nobody bothered solving it. There were some half-hearted attempts at doing it, but I had a feeling nobody bothered to do it seriously, including the police and people whose lives were affected by it. <br /><br />My own opinion: a decent book with nothing really outstanding. My rating is <b>2.5 stars</b> rounded up: I do not want to penalize the book for not belonging to my favorite genre. <br /><br />This review is a copy/paste of my LeafMarks one: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.leafmarks.com/lm/#/users/10968/books/18897/review">https://www.leafmarks.com/lm/#/users/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10778362789752032080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-werewolves-and-shifters">fantasy-werewolves-and-shifters</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759080302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14669227000939565204"><b>Original Rating: 5 stars<br/>New Rating: 2 Stars<br/><br/>This was a Buddy read (re-read for me) with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-oosarahoo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karly</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5892196-carole-s-random-life' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18711982-kristin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristin</a> (when we get to book 3), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kelly</a> (when we get to book 4), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7125124-jess' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jess</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine.</a></b><br/><br/>Ok, I don't know what I was thinking when I gave this book 5 stars. This is not a 5 star book. This was my 4th time reading this and I think my last. The main reason is: it's BORING. There was WAY too much Bill. I didn't realize how boring Bill was. I mean, he was always super boring compared to Eric, but </span>
  <span id="freeText14669227000939565204" style="display:none"><b>Original Rating: 5 stars<br>New Rating: 2 Stars<br><br>This was a Buddy read (re-read for me) with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-oosarahoo" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja" rel="nofollow noopener">Karly</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5892196-carole-s-random-life" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18711982-kristin" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristin</a> (when we get to book 3), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly</a> (when we get to book 4), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7125124-jess" rel="nofollow noopener">Jess</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine.</a></b><br><br>Ok, I don't know what I was thinking when I gave this book 5 stars. This is not a 5 star book. This was my 4th time reading this and I think my last. The main reason is: it's BORING. There was WAY too much Bill. I didn't realize how boring Bill was. I mean, he was always super boring compared to Eric, but he was a total snoozefest this time for me. (He favors Kenny G music for God's sake!) I think he actually said once to Sookie, "I wish to enter you again." What a cornball. Maybe it's supposed to be cute?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419983452ra/13152456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419983452ra/13152457.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Too much Bill, not enough ERIC NORTHMAN. The best scenes of the book were at Fangtasia and sadly that was only twice in this one. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419983452ra/13152458.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The series gets MUCH better when it moves away from Bill and toward ERIC.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419983452i/13152459.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sookie, outside of her telepathy, is just a boring Southern barmaid who wears banana clips and pines for a husband who will one day join the local Rotary club and grab milk for her on the way home from the office - when the sun's still shining.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419983452ra/13152460.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The murder mystery was quite dull as well. But at least we got to meet Bubba in this one!<br><br>I still recommend some of the later books (but not too much later because they get craptastic towards the end). This does kind of read like chick lit, though. I hadn't thought to put it in that category before. Previous to this series, Charlaine Harris wrote "cozies," so I think that small town mystery vibe comes through strong in this one. There is a lot more excitement in the next few books (through book 8 or 9, then the series fades quickly). It's really all about Eric Northman for me. </span>
